<name>Alyx Barranger</name><UserId.>106226941420364887072<//UserId.>< Text>
I really wanted to like this place when I came here, but in the end it was just okay.  I ordered pupusas and a carnitas burrito that I split with my fiance.  We both thought that they were solid, but there wasn't anything particularly special that made this place stand out.

I wouldn't mind coming back, but I don't think that you will be blown away by your experience here.  I'm probably spoiled from having been to some of the most incredible places in Sunnyvale that boast some delicious, authentic food.  I also didn't like the fact that they had so few seats!  Most people were left standing, and it was a little awkward eating pupusas along a narrow counter top while standing in my opinion.

Overall, this place was solid, but nothing that I would go out of my way to get.<//Text>

<Rate>3< /Rate>< Review>
Got two carnitas takeout burritos (they weren't just for me) here. La Bamba seems to do a very decent job with the food, but it's unexceptional relative to La Costena next door. The menu is rather limited and doesn't give the sense that items can be customized - they can. My super burrito was very light on the guacamole, but had a good balance of beans and carnitas. Still though, not quite as first-rate as the competition.

Another highlight for me was the horchata - really solid version filled with cinnamon goodness.

Definitely don't come for the ambiance. Get in, get your food, and get going.<//Review>

<rate>3</rate>< text>
[From June 2008]

ye, carumba.  Que lastima :-(.  I had such high hopes for this place, given all the raves, and I was sorely disappointed... especially since I took my never-eaten-a-burrito-before Aussie friend here today!

I already knew that parking and seating was limited, so I won't count that against this place.  Rather, here are the things that bummed me out:
- No choice of sizes (e.g., mini/baby burrito).
- No choice of salsas (I wasn't asked "hot or mild?" like at most taquerias I've been to).
- No salsa bar!  How can you have a taqueria without any visible salsa options?!
- No chips.  I'm used to getting free chips with my burritos (or better yet, chips with pico de gallo!)
- Tacos were a bit too greasy.
- Burrito was more cheesy than salsa'y :(.
- No seafood options (e.g., prawn burrito)
- No frescas? (e.g., watermelon, strawberry...)

But there were a few good things:
- Service was pretty fast.
- Cashier was friendly.
- They take credit cards.
- The carnitas was tasty... cooked just right!  El pastor was pretty good, too.
- Tortillas are grilled, not steamed.  Big thumbs up!

*  *  *

Still, I really miss La Corneta from Glen Park :-(</text>

Played here twice, Sunday 5/18 and 5/29.
Field is great.
By far the best MilSim field I've played in SoCal.
Player conduct reasonable to really professional w/the usual group or two of a-hole younger guys/teenagers who do not call their hits.
Cost is great at $20.00.
Only real negative is the referee(s) and some of the people who work here and what appears to be a group of their friends.
Individually, all nice people.
Collectively, they hang out together during and between games and seem more interested in their internal conversations than running a good game and a solid business
On Sunday 5/29, I think they were all hung-over: short-tempered, talked among themselves constantly, and a kiss-my-ass attitude from start to finish.

If I owned Warped Ops, I'd fire all of them and hire new people.
Guys, if you do not like your job at Warped Ops, quit and go do something else.  You have A LOT of guys playing here who are old enough to be your fathers...speaking to us and treating us with some measure of respect would be helpful. <Resp>None</Resp><name>D J<//name><time>1440938695857<//time>< review>
I've played at this field a fair amount so my opinion is averaged out over the course of many months.

Firstly, the field itself is fun, well laid out, with lots of brush everywhere. Though It lacks a lot of cover, as the field only has a few building, which are made of plywood. Not uncommon on an airsoft field, but when compared to SC Village, or Hollywood Sports it's lacking.

The staff is another story. They have moments of being courteous and professional, but many times I've seen them yell at players screaming profanity with many other young players present, I've seen them talk condescendingly to people asking for help, and most importantly I've seen them break the rules they stress so often. First and foremost, is the bias towards the regulars. Many times these "regulars" will join in reffing games, as well as operate the chronograph, and demonstrate bad sportsmanship without repercussions. Secondly is the lack of "reffing". They rarely solve disputes in a fair diplomatic way, if they do at all.

The players at this field is ultimately what drove me away. There is a good bunch of guys who play there by the rules, and to have a good time. Unfortunately there is a bigger group of "regulars" and others that come with chips on their shoulders, constantly complaining and treating the newer, and younger players with disrespect. They also show horrible sportsmanship, and make playing at this field frustrating. I've had players come up to me bragging about how their guns are shooting over the FPS limit, as well as cheating. Just recently I was physically attacked by another player for shooting him too closely, and I was immediately assumed to be the aggressor. That was the final straw, as my safety was jeopardized and has prompted me to write this review.

My opinion is if you're looking for a place to play airsoft in Los Angeles; FIND ANOTHER FIELD. Many first time players I've met over the year and a bit that I've played here have left dissatisfied and shocked at the lack of respect from the staff, and terrible sportsmanship of the other players. Airsoft is a sport of honor, and there's no honor in gung-ho people who treat others with disrespect from every angle at this field.< /review>

< text>
Awesome, field, great for all ages and skill level. This was the first field I've been to and i haven't had a better experiance anywhere else. The employees are very kind and friendly and work very hard to make sure their customers are having a blast. The referees are good. They constantly pay attention to make sure everyone is playing the game fairly and safely. However, there's sometimes scuffles between the players due to disagreements, as well as heavy swearing. The field is very safe as far as i've seen. It seems like the only true danger on the field is tripping and stuff, or being dumb enough to take off your mask/eye protection. Regardless, Warped Ops is no doubt the best airsoft field in Santa Clarita for organized, simple play.< /text>

<Review>This place is a very good field to play at, I hear that the refs curse but its fine by me, I don't mind them cursing, I even curse myself. I went there during the summer to get into airsoft and I even went to their 2nd night ops. I would have had a better experience at the night ops if my goggles didn't fog so that issue was on me. They always explain the rules, do's and don'ts, make sure to always follow the rules. Never, ever complain against the refs, because if you bring a gun that requires a 100ft minimum engagement distance and he just makes an estimate, just go with it, don't piss off the ref. I wish they could fit in at least 1 new game mode, Benghazi, king of the trenches, infected, team deathmatch, ambush, and most importantly Death Star are really fun game modes that I've played there. I'm currently getting a red dot for my SVU bullpup sniper rifle so I can make my experience playing a bit better for myself since I can't aim my iron sights because of a cheek riser. Anyways, I have fun playing at this field, I even asked a couple of guys if I could see their gun and they were also interested in seeing mine since it was rare to see a bullpup russian sniper rifle. The field has a great layout and I made multiple friends there at Warped Ops.<//Review><Pics>None<//Pics>< response>

< text>
Ive been to warped ops around 10 times or so over the past year. The field is great, the people there are very helpful. I have one problem here though thats stopped me from coming in the past. The amount of games played. Its partially the fault of players that play that day. not getting up or loading their guns fast enough. but mostly its the refs. I like all the refs, they can be sarcastic but they mean well. i just wish we could get more games in and start earlier. even tho theyre arnt alot of people at the field by 10 i think they should still do some pick up games while we wait for more! honestly thats my only con about this place. ive met alot of nice people who seem to go their regularly. the refs keep the teams balanced and the game modes they play and amazing and pretty immersive. over i give the place a 5 star. and if your a ref or the owner at warped, can you guys try to get more games in! thanks :)< /text>

<response>None<//response><Rate>4<//Rate><gmapID>0x80c27871d3f382d5:0xf7b7df841a458cdb< /gmapID><user_name>SlyFox9001</user_name><Review>Lengthy narrative but maybe worth the read ("Knowing is half the battle.") :
I've been to multiple fields as well as Milsim AO's. Warped Ops is probably my favorite semi-local outdoor field due to the variety of terrain (trenches, hills, small buildings), interesting game scenarios (King of the Trenches is fun), and exclusivity to airsoft (no paintball mess). I would say the field is geared for the more intermediate players as beginners may get worn out from the back-and-forth of a big field.

After reading the other reviews, it seems like staffing/reffing is the main subject of critique. I can say that the staff are strict and have zero tolerance for anyone breaking safety rules. People do get yelled at for removing eye protection on the field (Breaking rule #1). Better yelled at than losing an eye, I think. Also having a magazine in your gun in the parking lot is no good. I should know...

At the safety brief (mandatory to attend), the ref explains about what to do when someone doesn't call their hits/gets caught cheating: Try to remember the appearance of who you think is cheating and talk to the ref AFTER the round or when you yourself call "hit". They'll handle it from there! That's part of their job. Be composed. It's a game where adults shoot small plastic pellets at each other, sheesh! Please don't confront people yourself. Also please attend safety brief (it's very important!!)

In conclusion, if you're looking for an outdoor field and a chance to practice different strategies and tactics to complete objectives, and/or just have fun slinging bbs, Warped Ops is a great place to go. Never forget to bring water and hydrate often. The porta-potties are clean and maintained. The field is always growing and changing as far as buildings, terrain, quality of rentals, etc. Show up and see for yourself.<//Review>< time>

<user_name>Amy Hanoa</user_name><Date>1476866094274</Date>< rate>
5<//rate>
<text>Quickie:
+ If you love fish, you need to eat here
+ White fish plate, garlic butter, white rice (all day, son)
+ CALL AHEAD TO ORDER AND AVOID THE WAIT
+ If you get it to go, make sure to grab utensils (not included in your bag)

---

Food:
First timers, try:
- White fish plate with garlic butter (comes with coleslaw and bread)
- Spicy corn chowder (large size you can share between two people)

The dishes I've listed above are my faves. I eat probably too much of that... probably need to cut back on my fish consumption for a while. But the garlic butter is so good, I can't not get it... I know I should try something different but I know I love the white fish plate, so I stand behind it. I have tried the salmon and tilapia plates along with the grilled zucchini side and fish tacos too and they also taste yummy. But the white fish is my go-to.

Service:
This place is usually always crackin', especially at lunch time. Do yourself a huge favor and call in and place an order. Takes about 10-15 minutes then go to the second line that says "Pick Up Orders," avoid the huge line that stretches to the door. If you do walk-in and order, it can take up to 10 minutes to get your food if it's mega-packed. Just be forewarned...

Location:
The lot it's located in is jam-packed with other businesses so the parking can get hectic. I usually park as close to the entrance as possible so I can get out of there easier.

Verdict:
Great food, reasonable prices (about $8-$12 per plate) and good portion sizes. Very tasty menu and good selection. I'll be a regular for many years to come...<//text><pictures>None</pictures><Response>None</Response><gmap_id>0x80c2b561761fc3c9:0xc12661c66b4649dc<//gmap_id></record>

<userid>113581213966210971497< /userid><name>Amy Hanoa< /name><Date>1476866094274<//Date><rate>5<//rate><text>Quickie:
+ If you love fish, you need to eat here
+ White fish plate, garlic butter, white rice (all day, son)
+ CALL AHEAD TO ORDER AND AVOID THE WAIT
+ If you get it to go, make sure to grab utensils (not included in your bag)

---

Food:
First timers, try:
- White fish plate with garlic butter (comes with coleslaw and bread)
- Spicy corn chowder (large size you can share between two people)

The dishes I've listed above are my faves. I eat probably too much of that... probably need to cut back on my fish consumption for a while. But the garlic butter is so good, I can't not get it... I know I should try something different but I know I love the white fish plate, so I stand behind it. I have tried the salmon and tilapia plates along with the grilled zucchini side and fish tacos too and they also taste yummy. But the white fish is my go-to.

Service:
This place is usually always crackin', especially at lunch time. Do yourself a huge favor and call in and place an order. Takes about 10-15 minutes then go to the second line that says "Pick Up Orders," avoid the huge line that stretches to the door. If you do walk-in and order, it can take up to 10 minutes to get your food if it's mega-packed. Just be forewarned...

Location:
The lot it's located in is jam-packed with other businesses so the parking can get hectic. I usually park as close to the entrance as possible so I can get out of there easier.

Verdict:
Great food, reasonable prices (about $8-$12 per plate) and good portion sizes. Very tasty menu and good selection. I'll be a regular for many years to come...< /text>< pics>

<Resp>None< /Resp><pics>None<//pics><userid>104037524980967008271</userid><user_name>Kevin Gaines< /user_name>< Text>
First time visitor . . . certainly will be back.  Tired of taking Mom to P.F. Chang every time I visit L.A.  This joint is a short drive from her place.  Pretty simple; a limited menu, featuring various popular types of seafood, fried or grilled, with your choice of garlic butter sauce or cajun seasonings.  Add a choice of sides . . . brown or white rice, cole slaw, fries (sweet or regular potatoes).  I had the cajun salmon dinner, which featured 2 generous fillets.  Mom had the jumbo shrimp, with garlic butter sauce, which probably undid all the healthy choices she's made over the last couple months to drop almost 20 lbs.  Super delicious, though; both entrees.  If you'd rather go the baja route, a la Baja Fresh or Wahoo's, they do the fish taco/burrito thing too.  Their salsas taste really good

The atmosphere is big, casual and noisy . . . the restaurant interior kinda reminds one of a Chipotle store.  You order from the counter and have a seat.  You get your dish(es) very quickly after paying.  The best part of the experience, though?  $33 out the door, and that's only because Mom ordered the most expensive thing on the menu!

Good food, done fast, and pretty cheap.  Doesn't get much better.  Kudos, and see you again.<//Text>
